## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of time and velocity. In nonlinear oscillator systems, the acceleration typically depends on displacement (related to velocity via integration) and velocity through restoring forces and damping terms, often involving polynomial or trigonometric nonlinearities.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force (from displacement): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) (simple harmonic oscillator where position is sinusoidal)
- Linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (velocity-proportional damping force)
- Damped harmonic: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3) (damped oscillator with sinusoidal restoring force)
- Cubic nonlinearity (Duffing): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * sin(c1 * t)**3 (Duffing-type restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Van der Pol type: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (nonlinear damping with restoring force)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * v * abs(v) + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (drag proportional to v squared with restoring force)
- Polynomial restoring + damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 + c2 * v**3 (polynomial in velocity)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Combined nonlinear terms: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) + c3 * sin(c1 * t + c2)**3 + c4 * v (Duffing with damping)
- Power-law restoring: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t)**c2 (power-law nonlinear restoring force)
- Mixed polynomial-trigonometric: dv_dt = c0 * v**2 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c1 * t) (cross-coupling terms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Nonlinear restoring force → odd-power polynomial in displacement (sin(ωt) as proxy), e.g., sin³ or x + x³ (Duffing-type)
- Self-excited oscillation → velocity-dependent damping with sign change, e.g., (1 - v²)*v (Van der Pol structure)
- Phase-space structure → acceleration as function of velocity alone suggests autonomous system or limit cycle dynamics
- Periodic forcing/restoring → trigonometric functions of time sin(c*t), cos(c*t) indicate harmonic position dependence
- Amplitude-dependent frequency → mixing of different harmonic orders sin(ωt), sin(3ωt) from nonlinear restoring forces
- Energy-dependent damping → even powers of velocity multiplied by velocity (v³, v⁵) indicate nonlinear dissipation
- Conservative nonlinearity → acceleration depends only on position (sinusoidal function of time), no velocity terms
- Softening/hardening spring → cubic correction to linear restoring force with positive (hardening) or negative (softening) coefficient
